     9→import path from 'path'

    14→  
    15→const TEAMS_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro', 'teams')  
    16→  
    17→function ensureTeamsDir() {  
    18→  if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_DIR)) {  
    19→    fs.mkdirSync(TEAMS_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    20→  }  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→function tasksFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
    24→  // Validate teamId is a proper UUID to prevent path traversal attacks  
    25→  if (!/^[0-9a-f-]{36}$/i.test(teamId)) throw new Error('Invalid team ID')  
    26→  // Defense-in-depth: use basename to strip any directory components  
    27→  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${teamId}.json`))  
    28→}  
    29→  
    30→export function loadTasks(teamId: string): Task[] {

    37→    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')

  1034→// Format large numbers  
  1035→function formatNumber(num: number): string {  
  1036→  if (num >= 1000000) {  
  1037→    return `${(num / 1000000).toFixed(1)}M`  
  1038→  } else if (num >= 1000) {  
  1039→    return `${(num / 1000).toFixed(1)}K`  
  1040→  }  
  1041→  return num.toString()  
  1042→}

   100→  
   101→/**  
   102→ * Compute tmux session name from agent name and session index  
   103→ * Examples:  
   104→ *   ("website", 0) → "website"  
   105→ *   ("website", 1) → "website_1"  
   106→ *   ("23blocks-apps-backend", 0) → "23blocks-apps-backend"  
   107→ *   ("23blocks-apps-backend", 2) → "23blocks-apps-backend_2"  
   108→ */  
   109→export function computeSessionName(agentName: string, index: number): string {  
   110→  return index === 0 ? agentName : `${agentName}_${index}`  
   111→}  
   112→  
   113→/**  
   114→ * Derive display info from agent name for UI hierarchy  
   115→ * Splits on hyphens to create tags + shortName  
   116→ * Examples:  
   117→ *   "website" → { tags: [], shortName: "website" }  
   118→ *   "23blocks-apps-website" → { tags: ["23blocks", "apps"], shortName: "website" }  
   119→ */  
   120→export function parseNameForDisplay(name: string): { tags: string[]; shortName: string } {  
   121→  const segments = name.split(/-/).filter(s => s.length > 0)  
   122→  if (segments.length === 1) {  
   123→    return { tags: [], shortName: segments[0] }  
   124→  }  
   125→  return {  
   126→    tags: segments.slice(0, -1),  
   127→    shortName: segments[segments.length - 1]  
   128→  }  
   129→}  
   130→

   132→// Agent Session (Multi-Brain Support)

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:19:40]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Confirmed: On regular (non-forwarded) send success (line 231-239), the code does NOT call `fetchSentMessages()` or `fetchSentCount()`, unlike the forward success path (lines 207-209) which does call `fetchMessages()` and `fetchUnreadCount()`. This means the "Sent" tab will be stale after sending a regular message until the next 10-second poll cycle.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:18:26]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have all the information needed to write the report. Let me compile my findings.  

**Findings summary after thorough review:**  

1. **GovernancePasswordDialog.tsx (206 lines):**   
   - Line 95: The backdrop `<div>` does not have an `onClick` handler to close the dialog on backdrop click, which is inconsistent but not a bug per se.  
   - No Escape key handler for dialog dismissal (only Enter key handled on inputs).  
   - The `AnimatePresence` wrapping is correct; `exit` animation is properly defined on `motion.div`.  
   - State reset logic in both `useEffect` and `handleClose` is redundant but harmless.  
   - Confirm mode (line 80-83): calls `onPasswordConfirmed(password)` without `setSubmitting(true)` or try/catch. If the parent performs an async operation, there's no loading state in confirm mode. This is POSSIBLE since the parent (RoleAssignmentDialog) handles its own loading phase.  
   - `handleSubmit` is async, and the confirm branch (line 80-83) does not set submitting, so the button remains clickable during password confirmation. Multiple rapid clicks could call `onPasswordConfirmed` multiple times.  

2. **RoleAssignmentDialog.tsx (385 lines):**  
   - Line 206: Backdrop div does not close the dialog on click. The `motion.div` has `onClick={(e) => e.stopPropagation()}` (line 211) but no backdrop click handler exists.  
   - No Escape key handler for dialog dismissal.  
   - Line 108: `managerHeldByOther` is `string | false` (truthy string or false) due to `&&` operator. This is used as a boolean condition on line 316, which works correctly.  
   - Line 116-118: JSON.stringify comparison for team ID arrays works but is brittle - relies on sort() being stable. Since both arrays are sorted identically, this is fine.  
   - The `handleRoleChange` function (line 133-188) does sequential API calls in loops (lines 146-149, 154-157, 176-179). If any call fails partway through, the system is left in a partially-updated state. No rollback mechanism.  
   - Line 183-184: `onRoleChanged()` and `onClose()` called in sequence. If `onRoleChanged` triggers a re-render that changes `isOpen` to false, and then `onClose` is called, this is harmless since React batches state updates.  

3. **RoleBadge.tsx (69 lines):**   
   - Clean component. Proper conditional rendering between `button` and `span` based on `onClick` presence.  
   - Line 55: When `role === 'normal'` and `onClick` is undefined, returns `null`. This is documented behavior.  
   - No issues found.  

4. **TeamMembershipSection.tsx (294 lines):**  
   - Line 43: `e.target as Node` type assertion. If `e.target` is `null`, `contains(null)` returns false, which is safe behavior.  
   - Line 82: `closedSourceTeams[0]` - takes only the first closed source team for transfer. If agent is in multiple closed teams, only the first one triggers a transfer request. This could be intentional (simplification) or a logic gap.  
   - Line 64-69: `relevantTransfers` filter checks `transfer.agentId === agentId` OR `fromTeam?.chiefOfStaffId ===  

... [413 more chars truncated]

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

```json
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"

```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,

     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:17:35]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `message-filter.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/message-filter.ts",
  "offset": 1,
  "limit": 122
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { loadGovernance } from './governance'  
    11→import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    14→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    15→  recipientAgentId: string  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted

```json
{
```

**Result:**

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale/expired entries on every cache write to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    const now = Date.now()  
    47→    for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    48→      if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)

   132→export function updateTask(  
   133→  teamId: string,  
   134→  taskId: string,  
   135→  updates: Partial<Pick<Task, 'subject' | 'description' | 'status' | 'assigneeAgentId' | 'blockedBy' | 'priority'>>  
   136→): { task: Task | null; unblocked: Task[] } {  
   137→  const tasks = loadTasks(teamId)  
   138→  const index = tasks.findIndex(t => t.id === taskId)  
   139→  if (index === -1) return { task: null, unblocked: [] }  
   140→  
   141→  const now = new Date().toISOString()  
   142→  const wasCompleted = tasks[index].status === 'completed'  
   143→  const isNowCompleted = updates.status === 'completed'  
   144→  
   145→  tasks[index] = {  
   146→    ...tasks[index],  
   147→    ...updates,  
   148→    updatedAt: now,  
   149→  }  
   150→  
   151→  // Set timestamps based on status changes  
   152→  if ((updates.status === 'in_progress' || updates.status === 'review') && !tasks[index].startedAt) {  
   153→    tasks[index].startedAt = now  
   154→  }  
   155→  if (updates.status === 'completed' && !tasks[index].completedAt) {  
   156→    tasks[index].completedAt = now  
   157→  }  
   158→  
   159→  // Find newly unblocked tasks when a task is completed  
   160→  let unblocked: Task[] = []  
   161→  if (!wasCompleted && isNowCompleted) {  
   162→    unblocked = tasks.filter(t => {  
   163→      if (!t.blockedBy.includes(taskId)) return false  
   164→      // Check if ALL blockers are now completed  
   165→      return t.blockedBy.every(depId => {  
   166→        const dep = tasks.find(d => d.id === depId)  
   167→        return dep && dep.status === 'completed'  
   168→      })  
   169→    })  
   170→  }  
   171→

   173→  return { task: tasks[index], unblocked }

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:18:38]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I notice an edge case: Line 143 - `isNowCompleted = updates.status === 'completed'` is `false` when `updates.status` is `undefined` (no status change). But `wasCompleted` checks the existing task. If a completed task gets updated (e.g., description change only), `wasCompleted` would be `true` and `isNowCompleted` would be `false`. The `!wasCompleted && isNowCompleted` guard protects against this, so it's fine.  

However, there's a subtle bug: if `updates.status` is `undefined` but the task was already `completed`, the spread `...updates` at line 147 won't overwrite `status` (since `status` is `undefined` in `updates`). That's correct behavior.  

Let me also trace the `wouldCreateCycle` function logic more carefully.  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:18:39]*

**Result:**

   196→export function wouldCreateCycle(teamId: string, taskId: string, dependencyId: string): boolean {  
   197→  const tasks = loadTasks(teamId)  
   198→  const visited = new Set<string>()  
   199→  
   200→  function hasCycle(currentId: string): boolean {  
   201→    if (currentId === taskId) return true  
   202→    if (visited.has(currentId)) return false  
   203→    visited.add(currentId)  
   204→  
   205→    const task = tasks.find(t => t.id === currentId)  
   206→    if (!task) return false  
   207→  
   208→    // Check what this task blocks (tasks that depend on it)  
   209→    const blockers = tasks.filter(t => t.blockedBy.includes(currentId))  
   210→    return blockers.some(b => hasCycle(b.id))  
   211→  }  
   212→  
   213→  return hasCycle(dependencyId)  
   214→}  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:18:45]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The `wouldCreateCycle` function: we want to check if adding `dependencyId` as a blocker of `taskId` would create a cycle. That means we'd be adding `dependencyId` to `taskId.blockedBy`. So we need to check: can we reach `taskId` from `dependencyId` by following the "blocks" edges (reverse of blockedBy)? The function starts at `dependencyId` and walks forward through what it blocks, checking if it reaches `taskId`. This is correct.  

Now let me check `deleteTeam`'s path construction for path traversal. The `id` comes from the route parameter `[id]` which is URL-decoded but from a Next.js route. The concern is that `deleteTeam` directly uses `tasks-${id}.json` without UUID validation.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:18:57]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Confirmed: `deleteTeam` at line 310 does `path.join(TEAMS_DIR, `tasks-${id}.json`)` without any validation on `id`. While `task-registry.ts:tasksFilePath` validates UUID format and uses `path.basename`, `deleteTeam` in `team-registry.ts` does NOT. However, `deleteTeam` first does `teams.filter(t => t.id !== id)` which only proceeds if the `id` matches an existing team. Since team IDs are generated by `uuidv4()`, only valid UUIDs would ever match. But a crafted `id` that doesn't match any team would return `false` before reaching the `fs.unlinkSync` line. So this is safe by accident, but not defense-in-depth.  

Let me also check one more thing about the `message-filter.ts` -- specifically the edge case where sender is NOT in a closed team but is COS of a closed team.  

Looking at `message-filter.ts` line 52: `senderTeams = closedTeams.filter(t => t.agentIds.includes(senderAgentId))`. If a COS is listed in `chiefOfStaffId` but NOT in `agentIds`, they won't appear in `senderTeams`. But the validation in `team-registry.ts` auto-adds COS to `agentIds` (R4.6), so this should always be consistent. However, there's a defensive concern if data was manually edited.  

Let me also check if the `loadTeams` migration has any race condition issue since it saves without a lock.  

</div>

   194→export function loadTeams(): Team[] {  
   195→  try {  
   196→    ensureTeamsDir()  
   197→    if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_FILE)) {  
   198→      return []  
   199→    }  
   200→    const data = fs.readFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
   201→    const parsed: TeamsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
   202→    const teams = Array.isArray(parsed.teams) ? parsed.teams : []  
   203→  
   204→    // One-time idempotent migration: safe without lock because migration is append-only and convergent  
   205→    // Migration: ensure all teams have a type field (default to 'open')  
   206→    let needsSave = false  
   207→    for (const team of teams) {  
   208→      if (!team.type) {  
   209→        team.type = 'open'  
   210→        needsSave = true  
   211→      }  
   212→    }  
   213→    if (needsSave) {  
   214→      saveTeams(teams)  
   215→    }  
   216→  
   217→    return teams  
   218→  } catch (error) {  
   219→    console.error('Failed to load teams:', error)  
   220→    return []  
   221→  }  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:19:04]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The migration at line 213-214 calls `saveTeams(teams)` without a lock, and this `loadTeams()` is called from inside `withLock('teams', ...)` in `createTeam/updateTeam/deleteTeam`, but also called directly from other places (like `governance.ts:loadTeams()`). The comment says it's safe because it's idempotent and append-only, which is correct -- the worst case is two concurrent saves both setting `type: 'open'`, which converges.  

Let me now check for one more issue: the `message-send.ts` passes `toResolved.agentId` which can be an empty string to `checkMessageAllowed`.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:19:14]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

When `toResolved.agentId` is `''` (empty string, from line 146), the `||` operator will fall through to `toResolved.alias`. This is correct because empty string is falsy. So the filter gets either the alias or 'unknown'. Since the message filter checks if this ID is in any closed team (via `closedTeams.filter(t => t.agentIds.includes(recipientAgentId))`), an alias or 'unknown' won't match any team's `agentIds`, so the recipient will be treated as "not in a closed team". This means the filter can't enforce closed-team isolation for unresolved recipients. Let me verify this is a real issue.  

If a sender is in a closed team and tries to send to an unresolved recipient who is actually in a different closed team, the filter would pass because the recipient's alias won't match any `agentIds`. However, this only happens when the recipient can't be resolved (e.g., remote agents), so it's actually reasonable behavior -- you can't filter what you can't identify.  

Now I have enough data to write the report. Let me compile my findings.  

</div>

     1→import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     2→import { checkMessageAllowed } from '@/lib/message-filter'  
     3→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
     4→  
     5→// In-memory cache: avoids re-reading governance + teams files for every agent  
     6→// on each request. TTL of 5 seconds balances freshness with performance.  
     7→const cache = new Map<string, { ids: string[]; expiresAt: number }>()  
     8→const CACHE_TTL_MS = 5_000  
     9→  
    10→export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {  
    11→  try {  
    12→    const agentId = request.nextUrl.searchParams.get('agentId')  
    13→  
    14→    if (!agentId) {  
    15→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentId query parameter is required' }, { status: 400 })  
    16→    }  
    17→  
    18→    // Check cache first  
    19→    const cached = cache.get(agentId)  
    20→    if (cached && Date.now() < cached.expiresAt) {  
    21→      return NextResponse.json({ reachableAgentIds: cached.ids })  
    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    // Cache miss or expired — compute reachable agents  
    25→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    26→    const reachableAgentIds: string[] = []  
    27→  
    28→    for (const agent of allAgents) {  
    29→      if (agent.id === agentId) continue  
    30→      if (agent.deletedAt) continue  
    31→  
    32→      const result = checkMessageAllowed({  
    33→        senderAgentId: agentId,  
    34→        recipientAgentId: agent.id,  
    35→      })  
    36→  
    37→      if (result.allowed) {  
    38→        reachableAgentIds.push(agent.id)  
    39→      }  
    40→    }  
    41→  
    42→    // Store in cache with TTL  
    43→    cache.set(agentId, { ids: reachableAgentIds, expiresAt: Date.now() + CACHE_TTL_MS })  
    44→  
    45→    // Evict stale/expired entries on every cache write to prevent unbounded growth  
    46→    const now = Date.now()  
    47→    for (const [key, entry] of cache) {  
    48→      if (now >= entry.expiresAt) cache.delete(key)  
    49→    }  
    50→

     1→/**

     3→ *  
     4→ * POST /api/v1/route  
     5→ *  
     6→ * Routes a message to the recipient agent within the local mesh network.  
     7→ * This is the primary message-sending endpoint for AMP providers.  
     8→ *  
     9→ * Authentication:  
    10→ *   - Bearer token (API key) for direct agent requests  
    11→ *   - X-Forwarded-From header for mesh-forwarded requests from known hosts  
    12→ *  
    13→ * Delivery methods:  
    14→ *   1. Local delivery — file system inbox + tmux notification (agent on this host)  
    15→ *   2. Mesh forwarding — HTTP POST to peer host's /api/v1/route (agent on another host)  
    16→ *   3. Relay queue — store-and-forward when recipient is offline or unreachable  
    17→ *  
    18→ * External providers (e.g. crabmail.ai) are rejected with 422 — clients must  
    19→ * send directly to the external provider using its route_url from registration.  
    20→ *  
    21→ * Resolution flow:  
    22→ *   1. Mesh-forwarded request? → local-only lookup (loop guard: never re-forward)  
    23→ *   2. Explicit remote host in address? → trust it, forward directly  
    24→ *   3. Otherwise? → checkMeshAgentExists (local first, then all peers)  
    25→ *   4. Resolved remote? → forwardToHost() → queue on failure  
    26→ *   5. Resolved local? → inbox write + tmux notification  
    27→ *   6. Not found anywhere? → inbox write + relay queue

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation

    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts",

  "limit": 100
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:18:38]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good - the `finally` block at line 119-121 ensures `releaseLock()` always runs, even on early returns. That's correct.  

Now let me check a critical issue - the `resolveTransferRequest` at line 63 acquires a 'transfers' lock via `withLock`. But we're already holding the 'teams' lock. Let me verify these are different lock names and won't deadlock.  

The locks are `'teams'` (acquired at line 42) and `'transfers'` (used inside `resolveTransferRequest` at transfer-registry.ts line 98). Different names, so no deadlock. Good.  

However, there's a subtle issue at line 72-73: if the destination team doesn't exist after already resolving the transfer request (line 63 already marked it as 'approved'), the transfer request is marked approved in the transfers file but the team mutation never happens. This leaves the system in an inconsistent state.  

Let me also verify the `saveTeams` return value pattern.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:19:18]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now let me verify one more important thing. In the `resolve` route, the `resolveTransferRequest` function acquires a `'transfers'` lock. We are ALREADY holding the `'teams'` lock. `resolveTransferRequest` also calls `loadTransfers()` → `readFileSync()` on a different file. This should be fine since they're different locks and different files. But I want to check if any code path from `resolveTransferRequest` could try to acquire the `'teams'` lock.  

</div>

    92→export async function resolveTransferRequest(  
    93→  id: string,  
    94→  status: 'approved' | 'rejected',  
    95→  resolvedBy: string,  
    96→  rejectReason?: string  
    97→): Promise<TransferRequest | null> {  
    98→  return withLock('transfers', () => {  
    99→    const requests = loadTransfers()  
   100→    const idx = requests.findIndex(r => r.id === id)  
   101→    if (idx === -1) return null  
   102→    if (requests[idx].status !== 'pending') return null // Already resolved  
   103→  
   104→    requests[idx] = {  
   105→      ...requests[idx],  
   106→      status,  
   107→      resolvedAt: new Date().toISOString(),  
   108→      resolvedBy,  
   109→      rejectReason: status === 'rejected' ? rejectReason : undefined,  
   110→    }  
   111→    saveTransfers(requests)  
   112→    return requests[idx]  
   113→  })

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:19:25]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good. `resolveTransferRequest` only acquires `'transfers'` lock, no nested lock acquisition. No deadlock risk.  

Now let me examine the inconsistency I noticed: at line 63 in the resolve route, `resolveTransferRequest` marks the transfer as `'approved'` in the transfers file. THEN at line 72, if the destination team doesn't exist, it returns an error. But at this point, the transfer is already permanently marked as `'approved'` in the transfers registry. The team mutation was never performed, leaving data inconsistent.  

Let me also check if the `Content-Length` header check (line 302-308 of the v1 route) happens BEFORE `request.json()` (line 311). This is important because `Content-Length` can be spoofed.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:19:29]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The `Content-Length` check is only a header check. A malicious client can set `Content-Length: 100` but send a 10MB body. The actual body is still parsed at line 311 without size validation. This is a known limitation but worth noting.  

Now let me write the complete report.  

</div>

     1→#!/bin/bash  
     2→# AI Maestro - Version Bump Script  
     3→# Centralizes version management across all files  
     4→#  
     5→# Usage:  
     6→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh patch    # 0.17.12 -> 0.17.13  
     7→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh minor    # 0.17.12 -> 0.18.0  
     8→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh major    # 0.17.12 -> 1.0.0  
     9→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh 0.18.0   # Set specific version  
    10→  
    11→set -e  
    12→  
    13→# Colors  
    14→RED='\033[0;31m'  
    15→GREEN='\033[0;32m'  
    16→YELLOW='\033[1;33m'  
    17→CYAN='\033[0;36m'  
    18→NC='\033[0m'  
    19→  
    20→# Get script directory and project root  
    21→SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"  
    22→PROJECT_ROOT="$(dirname "$SCRIPT_DIR")"  
    23→  
    24→# Read current version from version.json  
    25→VERSION_FILE="$PROJECT_ROOT/version.json"  
    26→if [ ! -f "$VERSION_FILE" ]; then  
    27→    echo -e "${RED}Error: version.json not found${NC}"  
    28→    exit 1  
    29→fi  
    30→  
    31→CURRENT_VERSION=$(grep -o '"version": *"[^"]*"' "$VERSION_FILE" | cut -d'"' -f4)  
    32→echo -e "${CYAN}Current version: ${CURRENT_VERSION}${NC}"  
    33→  
    34→# Parse current version  
    35→IFS='.' read -r MAJOR MINOR PATCH <<< "$CURRENT_VERSION"  
    36→  
    37→# Determine new version  
    38→case "$1" in  
    39→    patch)  
    40→        PATCH=$((PATCH + 1))  
    41→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    42→        ;;  
    43→    minor)  
    44→        MINOR=$((MINOR + 1))  
    45→        PATCH=0  
    46→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    47→        ;;  
    48→    major)  
    49→        MAJOR=$((MAJOR + 1))  
    50→        MINOR=0  
    51→        PATCH=0  
    52→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    53→        ;;  
    54→    "")  
    55→        echo ""  
    56→        echo "Usage: $0 <patch|minor|major|version>"  
    57→        echo ""  
    58→        echo "Examples:"  
    59→        echo "  $0 patch    # ${CURRENT_VERSION} -> ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.$((PATCH + 1

```bash
# Check visual width of box top/bottom vs content lines
# The ═ is 3 bytes each (UTF-8), ╔/╗/╚/╝ are 3 bytes each, ║ is 3 bytes
# Line 65: ╔ (3) + 64×═ (192) + ╗ (3) + quotes/echo = 198+7
```

  1214→            IFS=',' read -ra GW_ITEMS <<< "$SELECTED_GATEWAYS"  
  1215→            for gw_item in "${GW_ITEMS[@]}"; do  
  1216→                local gw_display=""  
  1217→                case "$gw_item" in  
  1218→                    slack)    gw_display="Slack" ;;  
  1219→                    discord)  gw_display="Discord" ;;  
  1220→                    email)    gw_display="Email" ;;  
  1221→                    whatsapp) gw_display="WhatsApp" ;;  
  1222→                    *)        gw_display="$gw_item" ;;  
  1223→                esac  
  1224→                if [ -n "$gw_list" ]; then  
  1225→                    gw_list="${gw_list}\n- ${gw_display}"  
  1226→                else  
  1227→                    gw_list="- ${gw_display}"  
  1228→                fi  
  1229→            done  
  1230→            portable_sed "s|{{ACTIVE_GATEWAYS_LIST}}|${gw_list}|g" "$MAILMAN_DIR/CLAUDE.md"  
  1231→        fi  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:18:52]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

This is a potential issue: `gw_list` contains literal `\n` strings (not actual newlines). When passed to `sed`, the `\n` in the replacement string is interpreted differently by BSD sed (macOS) vs GNU sed (Linux). On macOS BSD sed, `\n` in the replacement is treated as literal `\n` (not a newline). On GNU sed, `\n` in the replacement is also treated as literal `\n`. Neither actually produces a newline in the output. This means the bullet list would appear as `- Slack\n- Discord` literally in the file, not as separate lines. However, this is an existing behavioral choice and the template file may be designed for this. Let me check if this is actually a problem worth flagging.  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:18:52]*

<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- Test sed behavior with backslash-n in replacement on macOS</summary>

**Input:**

*Test sed behavior with backslash-n in replacement on macOS*  

```bash
echo "test" | sed 's|test|a\\nb|g'
```

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 00:18:53  
a\nb  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:19:02]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

So on macOS, the `\n` in the `gw_list` variable will be treated by shell expansion as literal backslash-n, and sed will output `a\nb` literally. This means the CLAUDE.md file will get literal `\n` in the text rather than actual newlines. This is a bug -- the gateway list will appear as `- Slack\n- Discord` instead of as separate lines.  

Now let me verify whether the MAILMAN-CLAUDE.md template exists and how it's supposed to look.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:19:17]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `bump-version.sh`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/scripts/bump-version.sh",
  "offset": 100,
  "limit": 15
}
```

**Result:**

   100→update_file() {  
   101→    local file="$1"  
   102→    local pattern="$2"  
   103→    local replacement="$3"  
   104→    local description="$4"  
   105→  
   106→    if [ -f "$file" ]; then  
   107→        if grep -q "$pattern" "$file" 2>/dev/null; then  
   108→            _sed_inplace "$file" "s|$pattern|$replacement|g"  
   109→            echo -e "  ${GREEN}✓${NC} $description"  
   110→            FILES_UPDATED=$((FILES_UPDATED + 1))  
   111→        fi  
   112→    fi  
   113→}  
   114→  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:19:26]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The version pattern like `"version": "0.23.12"` has dots which are regex metacharacters. In `grep -q`, the dot matches any character, so `0.23.12` would also match `0X23Y12`. Similarly in `sed`, the dots in the pattern match any character. However, since this is used specifically for version strings, the practical risk of false matches is near zero (no version string in these files would accidentally match another pattern). This is a NIT at best.  

Let me check for one more thing -- the `update_file` function doesn't increment `FILES_UPDATED` if `grep -q` finds no match (the file exists but pattern not found). This means if bump-version.sh is run when the version was manually changed in some files but not others, it would silently skip those files. That's actually the correct behavior since the script checks patterns.  

Let me check the `set -u` status and any uninitialized variable issues.  

</div>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { loadGovernance } from './governance'  
    11→import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    14→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    15→  recipientAgentId: string  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }  
    45→

   200→  function hasCycle(currentId: string): boolean {  
   201→    if (currentId === taskId) return true  
   202→    if (visited.has(currentId)) return false  
   203→    visited.add(currentId)  
   204→  
   205→    const task = tasks.find(t => t.id === currentId)  
   206→    if (!task) return false  
   207→  
   208→    // Check what this task blocks (tasks that depend on it)  
   209→    const blockers = tasks.filter(t => t.blockedBy.includes(currentId))  
   210→    return blockers.some(b => hasCycle(b.id))  
   211→  }  
   212→  
   213→  return hasCycle(dependencyId)  
   214→}

    22→    }  
    23→  
    24→    if (agentIds && !Array.isArray(agentIds)) {  
    25→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'agentIds must be an array' }, { status: 400 })  
    26→    }  
    27→  
    28→    // Pass managerId for multi-closed-team constraint checks (R4.1)  
    29→    const managerId = getManagerId()  
    30→    // Load agent names to prevent team/agent name collisions (R2.1)  
    31→    const allAgents = loadAgents()  
    32→    const agentNames = allAgents.map(a => a.name).filter(Boolean) as string[]  
    33→    const team = await createTeam({ name, description, agentIds: agentIds || [], type, chiefOfStaffId }, managerId, agentNames)  
    34→    return NextResponse.json({ team }, { status: 201 })  
    35→  } catch (error) {  
    36→    // TeamValidationException carries the correct HTTP status code from business rule validation  
    37→    if (error instanceof TeamValidationException) {  
    38→      return NextResponse.json({ error: error.message }, { status: error.code })

   303→export async function deleteTeam(id: string): Promise<boolean> {  
   304→  return withLock('teams', () => {  
   305→    const teams = loadTeams()  
   306→    const filtered = teams.filter(t => t.id !== id)  
   307→    if (filtered.length === teams.length) return false

   312→    return true  
   313→  })

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 00:18:38]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have all the data I need. Let me check one critical detail: the `Team` type requires `type: TeamType` but the `makeTeam` helper in `validate-team-mutation.test.ts` and `team-registry.test.ts` doesn't set a `type` field by default.  

Let me verify the `Team` type field -- it's `type: TeamType` (required, not optional). The `makeTeam` in `validate-team-mutation.test.ts` at line 44-53 does not set `type`, and the `makeTeam` in `team-registry.test.ts` at line 60-69 also does not set `type`. This could be a type error, but let me check if TypeScript would catch this...  

Actually, looking at the Team type: `type: TeamType` is required. But these are test helpers creating objects with `...overrides` pattern. The object literal satisfies `Partial<Team>` requirement, not `Team`. The return type is `Team`, so this would be a type error at compile time. However, since this is a test with mock setup, the object may still work at runtime even if the `type` field is missing in the default. Let me check whether any test in these files actually uses `makeTeam` without providing a `type` override.  

Looking at `validate-team-mutation.test.ts`:  
- Line 144: `makeTeam({ id: 'team-1', name: 'Alpha Squad' })` -- no `type` set. This is used as `existingTeams` in `validateTeamMutation`. The function checks `t.type === 'closed'` so missing `type` means `undefined !== 'closed'`, which would make it behave as an open team. This is probably the intended behavior for that test.  

And in `team-registry.test.ts`:  
- The `makeTeam` is used only in `saveTeams` error test (line 117) where `type` doesn't matter.  

Now let me also verify that tests run correctly to confirm my analysis.  

</div>

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Interesting -- `document-api.test.ts` does NOT mock `team-registry`, yet the document API routes import `getTeam` from `@/lib/team-registry`. The `team-registry` module imports `fs` and `uuid` which ARE mocked. Since `team-registry` uses `import fs from 'fs'` (default import), and the fs mock in `document-api.test.ts` provides `default:`, the mock will work transitively. Let me verify the `createTeam` function used in the document-api test actually works with this mock setup.  

Looking at the mock in `document-api.test.ts` lines 9-21: it mocks `fs` with `default: { existsSync, mkdirSync, readFileSync, writeFileSync }`. This matches what `team-registry.ts` needs (uses `fs.existsSync`, `fs.mkdirSync`, etc. via default import). The `document-registry.ts` also uses `import fs from 'fs'` (default import).

In `team-api.test.ts`, `createTeam` is called directly at line 98: `await createTeam({ name: 'Team A', agentIds: [] })`. The `createTeam` function signature is `createTeam(data, managerId?, reservedNames?)`. Without passing `managerId`, it's `undefined`, and inside `createTeam` it does `managerId ?? null`. So `validateTeamMutation` gets `null` as managerId. This is fine for the open team tests.  

Now let me check one subtle detail: in `team-api.test.ts`, the POST route calls `getManagerId()` from governance (mocked to return `null`) and `loadAgents()` from agent-registry (mocked to return `[]`). This means the `reservedNames` array will be `[]`, which should be fine.  

Let me now also check a potential issue in the `task-registry.test.ts` -- the `assigneeAgentId` default. The source code at line 112 says `assigneeAgentId: data.assigneeAgentId || null`. If `data.assigneeAgentId` is `undefined`, then `undefined || null` is `null`. Good, test at line 213-216 verifies this correctly.  

However, there's a subtle issue: if `assigneeAgentId` is passed as empty string `''`, then `'' || null` is `null`, which would silently convert empty string to null. The test doesn't cover this edge case, but it's more of a missing coverage nit than a bug.

- Source at line 82: `assigneeName = agent.label || ag

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Task Registry - File-based CRUD for team task persistence  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Storage: ~/.aimaestro/teams/tasks-{teamId}.json (one per team)  
     5→ * Mirrors the pattern from lib/team-registry.ts  
     6→ */  
     7→  
     8→import fs from 'fs'  
     9→import path from 'path'  
    10→import os from 'os'  
    11→import { v4 as uuidv4 } from 'uuid'  
    12→import { loadAgents } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
    13→import type { Task, TaskWithDeps, TasksFile } from '@/types/task'  
    14→  
    15→const TEAMS_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro', 'teams')  
    16→  
    17→function ensureTeamsDir() {  
    18→  if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_DIR)) {  
    19→    fs.mkdirSync(TEAMS_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    20→  }  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→function tasksFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
    24→  // Validate teamId is a proper UUID to prevent path traversal attacks  
    25→  if (!/^[0-9a-f-]{36}$/i.test(teamId)) throw new Error('Invalid team ID')  
    26→  // Defense-in-depth: use basename to strip any directory components  
    27→  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`tasks-${teamId}.json`))  
    28→}  
    29→  
    30→export function loadTasks(teamId: string): Task[] {  
    31→  try {  
    32→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    33→    const filePath = tasksFilePath(teamId)  
    34→    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
    35→      return []  
    36→    }  
    37→    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    38→    const parsed: TasksFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    39→    return Array.isArray(parsed.tasks) ? parsed.tasks : []  
    40→  } catch (error) {  
    41→    console.error(`Failed to load tasks for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    42→    return []  
    43→  }  
    44→}  
    45→  
    46→export function saveTasks(teamId: string, tasks: Task[]): boolean {  
    47→  try {  
    48→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    49→    const file: TasksFile = { version: 1, tasks }  
    50→    fs.writeFileSync(tasksFilePath(teamId), JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  

</details>

   132→export function updateTask(  
   133→  teamId: string,  
   134→  taskId: string,  
   135→  updates: Partial<Pick<Task, 'subject' | 'description' | 'status' | 'assigneeAgentId' | 'blockedBy' | 'priority'>>  
   136→): { task: Task | null; unblocked: Task[] } {  
   137→  const tasks = loadTasks(teamId)  
   138→  const index = tasks.findIndex(t => t.id === taskId)  
   139→  if (index === -1) return { task: null, unblocked: [] }  
   140→  
   141→  const now = new Date().toISOString()  
   142→  const wasCompleted = tasks[index].status === 'completed'  
   143→  const isNowCompleted = updates.status === 'completed'  
   144→  
   145→  tasks[index] = {  
   146→    ...tasks[index],  
   147→    ...updates,  
   148→    updatedAt: now,  
   149→  }  
   150→  
   151→  // Set timestamps based on status changes  
   152→  if ((updates.status === 'in_progress' || updates.status === 'review') && !tasks[index].startedAt) {  
   153→    tasks[index].startedAt = now  
   154→  }  
   155→  if (updates.status === 'completed' && !tasks[index].completedAt) {  
   156→    tasks[index].completedAt = now  
   157→  }  
   158→  
   159→  // Find newly unblocked tasks when a task is completed  
   160→  let unblocked: Task[] = []  
   161→  if (!wasCompleted && isNowCompleted) {  
   162→    unblocked = tasks.filter(t => {  
   163→      if (!t.blockedBy.includes(taskId)) return false  
   164→      // Check if ALL blockers are now completed  
   165→      return t.blockedBy.every(depId => {  
   166→        const dep = tasks.find(d => d.id === depId)  
   167→        return dep && dep.status === 'completed'  
   168→      })  
   169→    })  
   170→  }  
   171→  
   172→  saveTasks(teamId, tasks)  
   173→  return { task: tasks[index], unblocked }  
   174→}  
   175→

   241→export async function createTeam(
